r R E F A C E . 



All who liavc attempted to solve tliose double 
Acrostics which are now so much in fashion know, 
to their cost, that much time and trouble must be 
expended in a search for words to which the initial 
and final letters are often a chief part of the clue. 
Much personal experience of this sort has led me to 
believe that an Acrostic Dictionary, in which the 
first and last letters of all words are arranged in 
Alphabetical order, will be a welcome and valuable 
addition to the solver's library. 

Acting upon this belief, I have gathered from 
authentic sources all such words as seem suited for 
Acrostic purposes, and have so arranged them that 
the eye can easily run down the lists of those which 
begin and end with any two letters. 

A composer has thus a full choice of st;ch words as 
he may require, and a solver can rapidly select those 
which seem likely to answer the conditions of a 
" light." 

Inflections have been omitted in most instances, 
although some few, such as paiticiples Avhich are used 
as adjectives, have been retained. Compound words 
in common use are given, and some foreign words 
which have been incorporated with our language are 
included in the list, as well as words lateiy coined, 



6 FEE FACE. 



wliicli are well suited for Acrostic purposes from the 
fact that they are Bot found in modern dictionaries. 

The task of compilation has heen necessarily long 
and tedious, but the result will doubtless be of con- 
siderable benefit to all who take pleasure in these 
verbal puzilles, which not only afford amusement 
combined with mental exercise, but also are an indirect 
means of acquiring much information of very varied 
character. 

If this effort meets with success I shall be encour- 
aged to prepare further lists of people and places, 
constructed upon a similar plan. 

PniLLrrpA M. Pearson. 

Drayton Pakslow Rectorv, 
1884.
